Municipal Supervisory Committee Requests Strict Punishment of You Bolu 101

You and the Five Police Officers Involved in the Incident Will Be Sent to the Court

The Supervisory Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters, in light of the fact that You Bolu, the chief of the Fifth District, ordered the shooting and killing of many enthusiastic anti-Japanese and national salvation masses, has paid great attention to the matter regarding official discipline. After sending personnel to investigate in detail and confirming the facts, the Committee specifically sent a letter to the Municipal Executive Committee, which was then forwarded to the Municipal Government, advocating strict punishment to appease public anger. The original letter is recorded below: "Regarding the incident in which police officers of the Fifth District Bureau of the Municipal Public Security Bureau shot and killed the public on the first of this month, resulting in a tragic incident, the matter is extremely serious. The Committee sent personnel to investigate the matter in detail and received a reply stating, 'Your office was ordered to investigate the Baoshan Road tragedy and conducted separate inquiries at the scene and other related parties yesterday. At about 6:00 PM on the first of this month, soldiers Hou Zhanyuan, Chuan Jisan, and Zhou Xiaoying of the Fifth Artillery Team of the Ministry of Railways were ordered to go out to conduct anti-Japanese propaganda and post slogans. The soldiers saw the police亭 at Baoshan Road and Qiujiang Road, which was clearly visible to the public, and immediately posted slogans. They were stopped by the patrol officer Guo Wenhan. The soldiers told him about their hatred for the destruction of the country and argued. Passersby watched and felt indignant about the matter, and some scolded the police officer as a slave who lost his country. At that time, the police officer struck the soldier's wrist with a baton and told them to leave quickly. The soldiers refused to comply and stuck the slogans on his body. They were then taken to the Fifth District Police Station. The masses were very dissatisfied and followed behind, gathering at the entrance of the Fifth District and refusing to disperse, requesting the bureau to punish the officer. The police also posted anti-Japanese slogans at the entrance of the Fifth District. Later, after being questioned by the district official, the soldiers were released. They stood on top of the car at the entrance of the Fifth District and reported that Guo, the district official, planned to dismiss the police officer tomorrow, and persuaded the masses to disperse. At that time, Comrade Yang Youren of the Sixth District also persuaded the masses to disperse, and the masses were satisfied. A portion of the people went north and south and dispersed on their own. A portion followed to the Sixth District Party Headquarters to quietly listen to the results of the negotiations. A portion remained and refused to disperse. They said that at about 2:00 PM that afternoon, three Japanese people went to the Fifth District Bureau and stayed inside for an hour, talking about something, and requested the district chief to report the details. Baoshan Road is an important thoroughfare for pedestrians. When people gather, those who pass by will inevitably stop and watch. As a result, the number of people gathered increased to about a thousand. At this time, Comrades Yang Youren and Feng Xiancheng of the Sixth District came again, inquired about the reason, and Feng Xiancheng introduced You Bolu to report the details to the public. Then, Comrades Feng Xiancheng and Yang Youren gave speeches to persuade the public to disperse. The public called You a traitor. At this time, a public bus from the North Station to Jiangwan also stopped to listen. Shi Tifen, an inspector of the bus company, urgently ordered the bus to leave, but the engine had stopped and could not start. The driver tried to find a way to start the car, but the public said that since the car had stopped, it should not be started again in the crowd. The driver was beaten by the public and rescued by Shi Tifen to the Fifth District. At this time, Comrades Yang Youren and Feng Xiancheng had already entered the crowd and persuaded everyone to disperse. The public was already showing signs of dispersing. At this moment, You Bolu, the chief of the district, ordered to open fire. The first order was issued, but the police officers did not fire. The district chief jumped up and shouted to open fire, and said that if they did not fire, their own lives would be in danger. So, live ammunition was fired, with more than twenty shots. Cai Yongfang and Shen Wanlin were killed. Cai was from Yuyao, Zhejiang, 22 years old. The bullet entered from the left back of his cheek and exited from his right temple, and he fell face down towards the north opposite the Fifth District. His family members were all farmers in his hometown, and he was a single man working as a bookbinder at Shiyongji Binding Workshop in Xingye Lane, Baotong Road, Shanghai. At 8:00 PM that afternoon, he finished bathing at the bathhouse at the southern end of Qiujiang Road, and encountered the Fifth District on the way. At this time, District Chief You ordered the police to open fire and unfortunately died. This person was usually honest and kind, and got along well with his friends. He had worked at Shiyongji for many years. Shen was from Zhenjiang, 18 years old. The bullet entered from his back and exited from his chest, and he fell face down towards the north in front of Yongtai Shop, 42 steps in a straight line from the Fifth District Bureau. He was an apprentice at Dali Military Uniform Shop on Baoshan Road. Five people were injured. Wang Xiangshou was shot in the back shoulder and out the front chest. Luo Fusheng was shot in the lower left back and out the front. Zhang Baolin was shot through the back and waist. Shen Xuekun was shot in the arm. Wang Hexing was shot in the left calf and the bullet did not exit. In addition, there are minor injuries who have not been admitted to the hospital, which are still being investigated. When asked, Dr. Sun Xiaoshan, the medical director of Jisheng Hospital, said that the bullets of those who were injured and sought treatment here all entered from behind, which proves that the public had already fled. As for Cai Yongfang, who died, the Fifth District Bureau reported to the Municipal Public Security Bureau yesterday that 'a pistol and three bullets were found on the deceased.' According to someone from a shop opposite the Fifth District Bureau (who asked to remain confidential), 'We did not sleep all night and watched the police officers pick up bullets and sweep up blood. At about 4:00 AM, they put a pistol inside the clothes of a deceased person in front of the shop.' According to Dong Guokai, the leader of the artillery team, 'After the tragedy occurred, I went to the scene and saw that the deceased appeared to be a worker in the store, lying face down with his hands and feet open. There were no guns or bullets, which can serve as proof.' Five police officers Lin Qingxiang, Qiao Xuechang, Liu Weicheng, Wu Maolin, and Lin Zhanyou said that they were forced to open fire by the district chief's second order. This is the situation of the tragedy. We should report the investigated situation truthfully. We respectfully ask you to examine it. According to this, when the whole country is resisting Japan and saving the country, and public sentiment is激昂, posting slogans is a very minor matter. The police officer failed to properly persuade them and detained people in the bureau, which aroused the righteous indignation of the viewers and gathered at the entrance of the Public Security Bureau, resulting in a serious situation. Although people were released and police were dismissed, it was inappropriate that a decision was not made beforehand. The public saw that the Japanese had stayed in the district bureau for an hour. What was the purpose? It aroused suspicion. They requested the district chief to answer. After explaining the details and being persuaded by Yang and Feng from the Sixth District, the public was about to disperse. There was no need to open fire to demonstrate. Even if there was a need to demonstrate, the first thing to do would be to fire a blank shot to warn. However, District Chief You Bolu issued an order when the public was about to disperse (as evidenced by the bullets all entering from behind), killing many people, disregarding human life, and perverting the law for profit. This is a heinous crime. Moreover, it was found that the district chief was dismissed due to a case when he was the previous branch director. According to the law, he should not be re-employed as a police officer in this city. Why was he still employed and promoted to district chief? This is difficult to understand. Correspondingly, we request your council to immediately forward this to the Municipal Government, to severely punish the district chief, in order to rectify officialdom and appease the public anger. We are extremely eager."

Another report states that at 8:00 PM on the first of this month, a conflict occurred between the public and the police on Baoshan Road, under the jurisdiction of the Fifth District, resulting in a tragic incident of gunshot wounds and deaths. After Mayor Zhang was notified, he immediately ordered the district chief You Bolu to be suspended from his duties and investigated. At the same time, he ordered Secretary-General Yu Hongjun to work with Municipal Party Committee member Wu Kaixian and Deputy Adjutant Jiang Yi of the Garrison Headquarters to thoroughly investigate the truth. The details were recorded in the previous newspaper. Now we know that Yu, Wu, and Jiang have completed their investigation of the incident and reported it to the Municipal Government, requesting that it be handled according to law. Mayor Zhang ordered that the district chief and the police officers involved in the incident be sent to the court for strict punishment.

All Circles Mourned Jiang Weishui Yesterday 102

The Painful History of Taiwan's Loss and Mr. Jiang's Struggle

Heartfelt Speeches by Representatives from Korea and India

Important Resolutions Passed by the Assembly

Yesterday (the 4th) morning at 9:00 AM, all circles in Shanghai held a memorial meeting for Mr. Jiang Weishui, the revolutionary leader of Taiwan, at the Penglai Grand Theater, Xiaoximen. It is estimated that over 600 representatives from more than 70 groups, including the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, the General Chamber of Commerce, the Postal Workers' Union, the United Federation of Korean Groups in Shanghai, the Indian National League in Shanghai, the Taiwan Compatriot Association in Shanghai, the Asian Cultural Association, the Chinese Vocational Education Society, the Chizhi College, the Quanzhang Middle School, and the Gongshi Middle School, participated in the memorial. The atmosphere at the meeting was extremely solemn. The presidium of the assembly included Huang Yanpei, Wu Mai, Huang Jiang Weishui's posthumous portrait

Jing Wan, Liu Shimu, Zhuang Xiquan, Shen Zhuowu, and Xu Jigong. After the music was played to start the meeting, the entire assembly stood at attention and bowed three times to the Party and national flag and the portrait of the Premier. Then, they bowed once to Mr. Jiang Weishui. After the presidium's Shen Zhuowu respectfully read the Premier's will, they were silent for three minutes to commemorate the Premier and to mourn Mr. Jiang Weishui, presenting wreaths. The chairman announced the purpose of the meeting, and Xu Jigong reported on the painful history of Taiwan's occupation by Japan. His words were extremely painful, stating roughly: "During the Sino-Japanese War of Jiawu, our country failed, and the Qing court sent Li Hongzhang to sign a peace treaty with Japan, including (1) the cession of Taiwan to Japan and (2) compensation of 30 million taels of silver. When the people of Taiwan heard this news, their hearts were filled with indignation, and they rose up in resistance. They organized an anti-Japanese group, and the people of the entire island armed themselves for self-defense. Although Japan had more than 30 warships, they could not land. After a standoff of Photograph of the memorial service for Mr. Jiang Weishui (taken by Penglai Photo Studio)

for two months, Japan had no choice but to protest to the Qing court again. Unexpectedly, the Qing government was weak and incompetent, and mentally deranged, and secretly presented a map of Taiwan to Japan. Japan was then able to occupy Taiwan. The compatriots of Taiwan have since become slaves of a conquered nation. After occupying Taiwan, Japan carried out massacres. The cruel methods of killing were such that engineers were first sent to survey the areas where Taiwanese people lived, then dug underground holes, and sent troops to drive the Taiwanese people into the holes to be buried alive. How could such cruelty be tolerated? For 37 years, the people of Taiwan have been under the iron heel of Japan. Mr. Jiang Weishui, the liberator of the people of Taiwan, died this year at the age of only 42. It is truly heartbreaking to speak of. Who will the future liberation of our Taiwanese people rely on? Relying on heaven, relying on earth, is useless. We must rely on our four million Taiwanese compatriots and the four hundred million compatriots of our motherland, 'working hard together to fight!'" Next, Zhuang Xiquan reported on the historical outline of Mr. Jiang Weishui. Mr. Jiang died at the age of 42, having been engaged in revolution for 20 years. He came from a medical school and studied Chinese politics with his classmates while at school. The Japanese principal often tried to stop him. Mr. Jiang argued with him, and the Japanese was moved to tears. After graduation, he was imprisoned for resisting Japanese political oppression. Whether it was the trial or the prison officials, they not only did not dare to show the slightest disrespect, but also expressed regret and admiration. Mr. Jiang's life's work included founding the Taiwan Minbao newspaper, organizing the Taiwan Cultural Association, establishing the Taiwan People's Party, the Taiwan General Labor Union, and the Taiwan Farmers' Association. His achievements were remarkable. However, in recent years, due to his opposition to Japan's use of poison to kill the indigenous people of Taiwan and Taiwan's opium policy, he offended the Governor-General of Taiwan, who disbanded the People's Party. After the dissolution, Mr. Jiang was exhausted, but continued to work hard. With the income from his medical practice, in addition to maintaining his personal life, he helped poor revolutionary comrades. People at the time compared his hard work to that of Gandhi. Mr. Jiang became ill and died as a result. Mr. Jiang's death was not from illness, but from the hands of Japanese imperialism." After the report, Wu Mai, the executive committee member and propaganda director of the National Lawyers Association and the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, read the memorial text, which stated roughly, "Alas, the ancestral land is not well made, entrusting the sea frontier to the island barbarians. It has been thirty-seven years since then, and the time is getting more and more dangerous. Looking at the slaughter of the captives, my heart aches and my liver is torn apart. If we do not speed up the rescue, we will be trapped in this predicament for a long time. ... I, the young man Mai, do not measure myself, but plan to wash away the national shame. I am determined to annihilate the Japanese pirates on the coast in the near future." Next, Huang Shaomei and Peng Ziming, representatives of the Asian Cultural Association, delivered memorial texts, which stated roughly, "Alas, the situation in Taiwan is bleak and dark. When the bad news came, my colleagues shed tears. The great enemy has not been destroyed, and the revolution has not been completed. The people are suffering, in a sea of fire. Return our rivers and mountains and restore their freedom. You, sir, took the lead, leading the entire Taiwan, actively opposing Japan, with sincerity and without separation. You never gave up, tasting gall. For twenty years, you also sponsored the organization of the New International, uniting small and weak nations and expanding anti-imperialism. You often said that our responsibilities are heavy, and that we must liberate the nation and achieve world harmony, so that we will not have lived in vain. Your words are still in our ears, but the sage has passed away. All who have blood and energy are saddened. The dead are gone, but their spirit lives on forever. Determining their legacy is up to future generations. Strive on, comrades, and make meritorious contributions, Taiwanese people. Continue to fight, continue to sacrifice, vow to destroy the great enemy, and complete the revolution. Today, we offer sacrifices to express our sincere heart. If you are conscious in the afterlife, come and enjoy it. Enjoy!" After the sacrifices, Mr. Huang Yanpei gave a speech, saying that Mr. Jiang Weishui was an unnamed Gandhi, a Gandhi who did not succeed. A truly famous Gandhi must have many unnamed Gandhis, and then Gandhi will succeed. What China needs at this moment is tens of millions of unnamed Gandhis, tens of millions of Mr. Jiangs, so that Mr. Jiang will not die and China will not perish. Then, Shen Zhuowu gave a speech, saying that we in China now need to resist. Whether male or female, we must resist, and we must resist our enemy, Japan. Next, representatives from the United Federation of Korean Groups, Park Chang-se and Kim Hong-seo, the president of the Indian League, Taylor St., and Wu Mai and Peng Ziming, all gave extremely heartfelt speeches. The two Koreans expressed deep indignation and pain at the Japanese occupation of the Eastern Province, stating roughly that the people of the province had been reduced to slaves of a conquered nation. If China does not rise up and fight to the death with Japan, it will soon perish as well. We, the oppressed peoples, must unite and overthrow Japanese imperialism. Finally, the assembly passed important resolutions: (1) Request the government to clearly order military and police agencies not to arrest Taiwanese, Koreans, and other small and weak nations and send them to Japan and other authorities; (2) According to the Premier's instructions to assist small and weak nations, request the government and compatriots from all walks of life to sponsor Taiwanese comrades in Shanghai in establishing Weishui School as a revolutionary memorial. After the resolutions were passed, they shouted slogans, played mournful music, and when the meeting ended, it was already 1:30 PM.

Japanese Man Drives Car Late at Night to Steal White Cloth Banners 103

Equipped with a Lifting Ladder on the Car

Stealing Cloth Banners from Various Roads

Around 1 a.m. yesterday morning, two Japanese men, driving a privately owned grayish-yellow car equipped with a ladder-like structure, stole and tore down white cloths and various anti-Japanese slogans posted at key road intersections along Jing'an Temple Road and Route Say Zoong, as well as those pasted on the walls of thoroughfares. Subsequently, the two Japanese men drove the car to Kangjia Bridge Alley, where they spotted a white bamboo cloth banner hanging diagonally near the corner of Longquan Garden. The Japanese men attempted to tear it down again, but a crowd of passersby grew larger and larger. Witnessing this barbaric behavior, they were all filled with indignation and were about to step forward to reason with them. Fortunately, nearby patrol officers heard the commotion and arrived in time to stop the two Japanese men. Realizing their plan had failed, the Japanese men jumped into the car, accelerated to full speed, and sped off westward.

Robbery in Broad Daylight on Tongfu Road 104

Two Handguns Stolen

Victims All Tied Up

Yu Wenjun, residing at No. 9, Lane 4, Huacheng Li, Tongfu Road, works at Dafeng Real Estate Company, No. 21 Yuanmingyuan Road. Around 10 a.m. yesterday morning, five robbers suddenly arrived, four of whom were armed with handguns. They broke in through the back door and tied up all thirteen men and women, including the tenant Chen Guirong, who lived in the same house, using torn bedsheets as ropes. They were all imprisoned in the rear room on the lower floor. Then, the robbers went upstairs, entered the rooms, rummaged through chests and cabinets, and robbed for about forty-five minutes. They stole jewelry, including jadeite and diamond ornaments, worth over four thousand yuan, along with over one hundred yuan in cash, and fled without a trace. Chen Guirong, who lived upstairs, was a member of the Shanghai Municipal Council Police Department. One of his handguns was also taken away by the thugs. Also, when the robbers were committing the robbery, Chen's friend, Special Constable Cai Tonggui, came to visit Chen. As soon as he entered the main gate, he was held by two robbers acting as lookouts. They disarmed him of his handgun and then drove him into the inner room, where he was imprisoned together with the others. Therefore, in addition to the silver and jewelry, the robbers obtained two handguns. It is said that the robbers were all young in appearance, with one wearing a Western suit as the leader. The others wore long gowns and short jackets of various styles. When they entered the door, they shouted that they were looking for Yu, and then they entered the hall, tore up the bedsheets on the bed, turned them into strips of cloth, and tied up the hands and feet of all the men and women in the house, so the victims had no way to ask for help. It is reported that the stolen items were mostly jewelry, including three pairs of gold-inlaid jade auspicious ornaments and a jadeite-inlaid diamond ornament, of considerable value. Upon hearing the news, the Xinzha Police Department immediately dispatched detectives to the scene to investigate and apprehend the suspects.

Disaster Relief News from Various Provinces 105

Jiangsu Flood Relief Association News

Survey of Shaobo Town and Various Villages: The association recently received a telegram from Yuan Jimei, acting on behalf of the Yangzhou office, providing a detailed report on the disaster situation in various villages of Shaobo. The original telegram is recorded below. On September 30th, Jimei, accompanied by relief workers Zhou Junliangji and Zhao Yisun, among others, carrying twelve bundles of relief clothing donated by all sectors of Suzhou, totaling over two thousand pieces, and three hundred pieces of various medicines, personally went to various villages in Shaobo to investigate. They arrived in the town at 11:00 a.m., led by Zhou Maosen and Geng Yuting of the World Red Swastika Society, and Sun Jiuru of the Chamber of Commerce, among others. They rested at the Zhongnan Hotel for a short time and then went to inspect the disaster situation in the South Street of the town. From South Pond Small Street and the left and right firewood dams to Bao Gong Temple, everything was washed away by the water, a vast expanse of water. They then took a charity ferry to Bao Gong Temple to inspect. They saw that there were still over thirty families in the temple, about one hundred disaster victims taking refuge inside. Another thirty or so families were taking refuge below Bao Gong Temple. All the houses were completely washed away by the water, and they had nowhere to go. They ate two meals a day, relying entirely on the town's porridge kitchen to survive. They also inspected North Street, and the situation was even worse than South Street. Countless houses were washed away by the water along the way. All the streets had become a pile of rubble. Along the street, only reed mat sheds were seen, all temporary shelters for disaster victims. There were eight breaches in the dike in front of the South Street Guan Yi Post Station, resulting in dozens of deaths and injuries. There were seven breaches in the dike in North Street, resulting in over three hundred deaths and injuries. Currently, there are about 1,300 disaster victims in the town and nearby areas. The Shaobo Flood Relief Association has established three porridge kitchens to help the disaster victims survive. One is located in the Town God Temple in the town, serving porridge to about 700 disaster victims every day. The second is located in the Zhongdao Wenchang Palace, serving about 400 people every day. The third is located in the Nandutian Temple, serving about 300 people every day. It is estimated that the three kitchens need about six shi of rice per day, with each person receiving about five he of rice per day. Currently, local impartial gentry have hired two charity ferries at the washed-away area of South Pond to facilitate the passage of disaster victims. There is a large bridge from Bao Gong Temple to South Street, which was broken by the water. It is planned to repair it and restore it to its original state so that the disaster victims on the opposite bank can travel back and forth. They discussed with Zhou Maosen, Geng Yuting, and Zhao Yisun to establish porridge kitchens in Qishu, Yong'an, Xiaqiao, Zhenwu Temple, and along the He Village, so that the disaster victims in each village can obtain food nearby, which would be most convenient. Moreover, Sun Jun Jiuru and Zhou Jun Maosen of the Chamber of Commerce consider it especially important to distribute reed mats for the disaster victims to build reed sheds for shelter. From south to north in Shaobo Town, there are dozens of breaches in the dikes, with the most severe disaster areas being from Zhuxiangkou Yang Mujian Wharf in the south to Guan Yi Post Station in the north, which is extremely tragic. The town is exceptionally filthy, with flies and insects filling the entire town, probably exceeding the number of China's 400 million compatriots. This matter is extremely noteworthy. If measures are not taken quickly to clean it, it will be extremely harmful to the hygiene of the people in the town. In the afternoon, accompanied by Zhang Bin, the village head of Qishu Town, and others, they took a boat from Ai Ling Lake all the way to the villages of Xiaqiao 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5 to survey. The fields on the left and right were indistinguishable from the lake, forming a vast expanse of water. When the boat arrived at Xiaqiao Village, over twenty small boats carrying disaster victims, old and young, came forward, surrounding and begging for relief. They comforted them with kind words and then proceeded forward, finally reaching Qishu Village. They saw that the embankments on both sides had completely collapsed. The breach in the left-hand side dike directly rushed towards the eastern end of Guangfeng Dike on the opposite bank. The water washed into the Xiahe area of Xinghua, where about 100 families lived in Guangfeng Dike. The houses were washed away by the water. Later, the disaster victims built reed sheds on both banks to shelter themselves. At a little after 5:00 p.m., they arrived at Qishu Town and saw about 1,000 disaster victims on both banks, with about 300 families. Nine-tenths of the houses were washed away, and the remaining houses were still in the water. In the middle of the river, there was a large bridge, which was also washed down, preventing passage to the opposite bank. When the boat arrived in the town, the disaster victims on both banks cried out for help, and the tragic situation was witnessed. All colleagues were heartbroken and shed tears. After the inspection, they immediately returned to Shaobo Town, which was already past 8:00 p.m. (omitted below)

Situation of Reception Centers and Porridge Kitchens in Jiangdu: The association's Yangzhou office reports that the reception centers have now been handed over to the Jiangdu Investigation and Release Bureau of the National Government's Flood Relief Committee Disaster Area Work Group. It has recently been actively preparing to establish porridge kitchens and has received the support of local gentry Zhao Yisun, Geng Yuting, and Zhou Maosen. The original telegram is as follows: From September 1st to September 20th, our office established seven reception centers, accommodating over 10,000 people. All expenses for rice, dry food, firewood, reed mats, and other miscellaneous items needed in the centers were allocated by our office. From September 21st, they have been handed over to the Jiangdu County Investigation and Release Bureau of the National Government Flood Relief Committee Disaster Area Work Group. Because the disaster situation in the Eighth District of Jiangdu County, Shaobo, such as Qishu, Yong'an Xiaqiao, Zhenwu Temple, and He Village, is extremely severe, it is proposed to establish porridge kitchens in each village on the spot, which is simpler and more convenient than setting up reception centers in the city, and disaster victims can definitely obtain real benefits (omitted below).

Disaster Situation in the Eastern and Western Villages of Baoying: The association recently received a telegram from Chen Huichen, acting on behalf of the Baoying office, stating that he had conducted a detailed survey of the eastern and western villages yesterday. In the eastern villages, such as Wangzhigang, Sheyang, Xian 、Juexi, etc., villages and settlements are sparsely populated, with nine out of ten houses destroyed, with people either taking refuge on high ground or going to other places. In the western villages, such as Jiaji, etc., the water in the fields is seven chi deep, with scattered farmhouses, completely dilapidated. The accumulated water has not receded, forming a vast expanse of water. The disaster area is expanding, the number of disaster-stricken households is increasing daily, and the scene is desolate, with intermittent cooking smoke. If the destroyed embankments of various companies are not urgently restored, not only will counties such as Xingdong suffer the same fate of being submerged, but the eastern and western villages of Baoying will also have no hope of planting wheat. The great disaster that is coming in the future, how can it be imagined? The rescue operations have just concluded, focusing solely on reception, and those transported to Jiangnan are even more continuously flowing. Urgent relief will be carried out in the coming days. The water route is vast, scattered and sporadic, making it difficult to investigate households and impossible to do so quickly. Relief funds are urgently needed in large amounts to provide thorough relief. The disaster situation in the county is evident.

A Live Drama of Catching an Adulterer 106

First Stealing the Adulteress's Clothes

Then Both Were Bound Up

Planning to Extort Money Through Mediation

Suddenly Discovered and Arrested by the Police

Feng, the wife of Zhao Baocai, a native of Yancheng residing at No. 324 Dongjiaxing Road, is 29 years old, from Yangzhou, and is quite promiscuous. She has been having an affair with Shi Xiaonian, a native of Changzhou residing at No. 63 Miller Road, for four months, but Zhao did not know. The night before, Shi Xiaonian took the opportunity to go to her place for a secret rendezvous, expecting that her husband would definitely not return home. However, someone informed Zhao Baocai, who then gathered his fellow villagers Wu Xuejin, Li Baowen, etc., and secretly went to catch the adulterers around 4:00 a.m. At that time,

A Pair of Lovebirds, Both Naked, Were Sound Asleep. First, Wu Xuejin quietly entered the door and stole her clothes, handing them over to Zhao Baocai to hold as concrete evidence of her adultery. Zhao had always been afraid of his wife and did not dare to act. After a while, Feng woke up and tried to get her clothes to put on, but could not find them. She was surprised and suspected a theft. Shi Xiaonian heard this and jumped up, shouting "Catch the thief!" Zhao, Wu, Li, and others burst into the bedroom and used ropes to bind up the adulterer and adulteress together. First, they pawned Shi Xiaonian's clothes at a pawnshop for nine yuan to pay for the cigarettes and alcohol for those who had helped. Zhao Baocai then extorted a large sum of money from Shi Xiaonian, saying that he would only drop the matter if he paid up, otherwise he would send him to the authorities. Shi had no money and was imprisoned in the room. Wu Xuejin's wife, Wang, acted as an intermediary, going to Shi Xiaonian's house on Miller Road to get money. Unexpectedly, this was discovered by Hou Fulin, a Chinese detective of the Harbin Police Station, who reported to the police chief and,

Together with a Western Detective, Rushed to the Scene and Arrested the Four Men and Women, Wu Xuejin, etc. They first retrieved Shi's clothes from the pawnshop at No. 316 on the same road, ordered him to put them on, and had Feng's clothes given to her by her husband. All were taken to the police station separately and detained. Yesterday, they were sent to the Third Criminal Division of the First Special Court. Zhang Tianyin, the police station's lawyer, stated that the case was complicated, and the police station accused the defendants of crimes such as obstructing freedom, intimidation, theft, and adultery.

He requested that they be punished according to the law and described the details of the case. Then, Central and Western Detectives Ming Yi presented a detailed account, including the clothes and a rope. Wu Xuejin confessed that Zhao Feng and Shi Xiaonian had been having an affair for a long time, and that her husband Zhao Shicai had caught them in the act last night. He denied stealing her clothes and binding her or pawning the clothes. Li Baowen confessed that Zhao had invited him to catch the adulterers, and the rest of his testimony was the same. Zhao Baocai confessed that he did not know that his wife Feng was having an affair with Shi Xiaonian. Last night, when he came home, he saw them sleeping together. He was so angry that he asked Wu Xuejin and Li Baowen to help him bind Shi. He denied the rest. Wu Wang confessed that after Shi Xiaonian was bound, she asked her to go to his house to borrow silver from a friend, but she did not find him, so she returned. She asked for Zhao Feng's confession. Zhao Feng admitted that she had been having an affair with Shi for four months, and the rest of her testimony was evasive. Shi Xiaonian confessed that he,

Had an Ambiguous Relationship with Feng for Several Months. Last night, he happened to be sleeping at her house when Zhao Baocai and others, including Wu and Li and others who were at large, came to catch the adulterers, bound him, and demanded money. Later, Wu Wang persuaded them to settle the matter peacefully. Judge Shen Bingrong verified the testimonies and declared to Zhao Baocai, "Do you want to prosecute Feng and Shi Xiaonian for adultery?" Zhao said that he did not want to pursue the matter. Judge Shen then ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody separately for sentencing on a fixed date.

Changes to the Motorized Bicycle Donation Payment Method 107

Announcement by the Municipal Public Utilities and Finance Bureaus

The donation for motorized bicycles in the city was originally set at five yuan per quarter. Due to the narrow body of the bicycles, it was impossible to affix donation plates separately, and only stamps were affixed to the four-season columns of the driver's license as proof. Recently, it has been heard that the Municipal Public Utilities and Finance Bureaus have found that many car owners who have obtained licenses have not paid the quarterly donations and have been riding in a mixed manner. Because there is no identification on the car indicating whether the donation has been paid, and inspecting the licenses of each car is considered troublesome and inconvenient, the inspection is extremely difficult. It is necessary to find a way to remedy this in order to increase the donation revenue. Therefore, after consultation between the bureaus, it is planned to change the motorized bicycle item to an annual donation, following the example of bicycles, with an annual donation of twenty yuan per catty, paid annually, and the license plate will be changed every year without additional charges. If the car owner stops riding after paying the donation, the overpaid donation will be refunded according to the number of overpaid months, calculated at an average of 1.66 yuan per month when the license plate is returned. Those who register and pay the donation after January of each year will also be calculated monthly from the month of donation to the end of the year, so as to be fair and convenient for verification. The change will be implemented from 1932. The bureaus have jointly submitted the plan to the municipal government for approval. Yesterday, the bureaus have announced the plan and issued separate orders to the Public Security Bureau for verification.

Observatory 114

Newly Appointed Father Li Takes Over

Father Qi Returns to the Meteorological Observatory

Father Li, who succeeded Father Lao as the director of the Xujiahui Observatory after his retirement due to old age this summer and returned to France, arrived in Shanghai on the Queen of Canada on the first of this month and took over the post at the observatory. Father Qi, who had been acting as director, returned to manage the affairs of the meteorological observatory. Father Li has a doctorate in science and graduated from the Department of Mathematics and the Department of Physics at the University of Paris Sorbonne. He also graduated from an electrical college. During the European War, he served in the artillery and radio teams. After the armistice, he devoted himself to celestial calculations. He first came to Shanghai in 1926 to prepare the Xujiahui Observatory's longitude calculation equipment. The following year, after the work was completed, he returned to France and specialized in the new method of measuring the earth's gravity and the automatic recording method of star luminosity at the Paris Observatory. He attended the International Astronomical Soil and Radio Conference. This time, he brought with him instruments for measuring the amount of ozone in the upper atmosphere and a recorder for studying the relationship between static electricity radio and meteorology. He is currently working on installing them. After they are put into use in the future, with Father Li's academic ability and the new meteorological research equipment, he will definitely open up a new chapter in the origin of hurricanes and weather forecasting, and add luster to the observatory.

Collision Between Car and Tram 115

Around noon yesterday, Tram No. 12 of the China General Tramway Company was traveling on Dongmen Road when a freight car of the China Chemical Industrial Company, No. 444 North Henan Road, simultaneously traveled south from the north. When they reached the intersection, the car tried to go first, but the tram had already arrived. The drivers of both vehicles were unable to avoid each other, causing the fronts of the two vehicles to collide with a loud crash. The front of the car was completely damaged, and the wheels were swept under the tram, while the body of the tram and the safety boards were also damaged. The fronts of both vehicles were immediately unable to move, causing traffic to stop. The police arrived and took the freight car driver, Chen Jinquan from Zhenru, along with the tram personnel to the district police station for preliminary examination and handling. After the China General Tramway Company heard about it, they immediately dispatched workers to the scene to remove the car wheels from under the tram and then drove the tram back to the company for repairs. Traffic gradually resumed, but the traffic had been stopped for several minutes.

A Woman with a Hard Life 116

Sold Several Times

Twice into Prostitution

Du Laxiang, a policeman from the Second Precinct of the Second District, found a young woman wandering on the road in Ximen South around 11 p.m. the night before. Suspecting her, he questioned her. She claimed that she had just come to Shanghai from Nanjing, had no relatives, and had no family. Fearing that she would be abducted by wicked people, he took her to the police station. She confessed that her name was Han, 23 years old, from Anhui. When she was three years old, she was abducted and sold to a Du family in the county as a granddaughter. Before a year had passed, Du's wife resold her to a Li family, who took her to Zhengzhou, Kaifeng, and other places. Later, she was sold to a Sun family in Jinan, who sent her to a brothel for about three or four years. She escaped to the Kaifeng Relief Society and married a Hu from Zhejiang. He took her to Guangdong. After more than a year, Hu was ordered to leave and arranged for her to wait at his brother's house. However, after a long time, she did not receive a letter. She moved out and made a living selling herself in that area for about half a year. She then married Liu Yaoqi from Xuzhou and came to Nanjing together. After living together for about three or four years, Liu left several months ago and never returned. Helpless, she went to Zhenjiang to look for him, then transferred to Suzhou, and then came to Shanghai, but still could not find him. She sighed at her hard life. The woman had a shaved head, gold teeth, a red shirt, and black pants. It was decided to send her to the Public Security Bureau for relief.

Zhang Xianqi Killed by Car 117

Zhang Xianqi, a native of Jiangbei, 19 years old, residing at No. 492 Meizhou Road, Yangshupu, set up a cake stall under the Xu Gaoxing teahouse at No. 502 on the same road. Yesterday afternoon, around 5:00 p.m., while riding a bicycle at the intersection of Pengpu Road, he was suddenly hit by Public Car No. 15078 on Jiujiang Road and knocked to the ground, causing the wheels to run over his abdomen and breaking both legs. He died on the spot. The Fire Brigade used a vehicle to transport the body to the Tongren Hospital for transfer to the coroner's office for examination.

Suzhou Child 118

Wang San-nan Lost, Awaiting Claim

Yesterday (the 4th) at 1 PM, a child of about twelve or thirteen years old was seen wandering and crying in front of the third district party branch of the Tianhou Palace in this city. The executive committee member of the district party branch immediately ordered the gatekeeper to bring the child inside to inquire about his origins. It was then learned that he was a lost child. According to the child, his surname is Wang, his given name is San-nan, and he is currently thirteen years old. His home is at No. 3 Jindao Bridge in Suzhou City. His father has passed away, and his family currently consists of his elderly mother in her fifties, and an older brother and sister. His brother's name is Fushou, he is currently seventeen years old, and works as an electrician in Suzhou, etc. After inquiring, the district party branch prepared a letter and sent it to the China Women and Children Relief General Association for temporary care. At the same time, a registered letter was sent to his family in Shanghai to claim him. Unexpectedly, after accepting the child, the Women and Children Relief Association suddenly sent the child back. Because it was already late, the child was temporarily kept at the party branch.

Reader Communications

A Certain Gentleman Asks (Regarding. Jiujiang. Resistance. To. Japanese. Goods. Not. Effortful) 126

Japan uses barbaric and strong means to brutally abuse our compatriots. Everyone with blood and spirit is furious. However, the anti-Japanese association in Xun is unique in its courage. The five-minute heat has passed. The inspectors from various gangs do not pay attention to the import of Japanese goods at all. In particular, the great silk gang uses a certain excuse to not send people to join. Its intentions can be imagined. Alas, if all places are like the treacherous merchants in Xun, the demise of our country can be expected immediately. The country is in a time of difficulty, and the future is long. Please publish this letter in your newspaper so that the merchants of Jiujiang can read it. It should be a wake-up call to gather a general meeting and start working seriously from now on.

A Certain Gentleman Asks (Regarding. Liuhe. Resistance. To. Japanese. Goods. Not. Effortful) 127

I live in Liuhe Town, which is dozens of miles away from Shanghai. The town is densely populated and there are many shops, but the people's knowledge is not very open. The shops display Japanese goods, which are everywhere. Once I went to a shop to buy a glass, but I saw that the trademarks were all Japanese goods. I asked the shop owner if there were domestic glasses for sale. He replied, "There are no domestic glass glasses." I was angry and returned. The other day, the vegetable shop came to my house to settle the bills. I said to him, "The Japanese have already occupied our three northeastern provinces. The country is about to perish. I advise you not to buy or sell Japanese goods, such as scallop shells and dried shrimps." He said, "What Japanese goods are not Japanese goods? We don't care about the three northeastern provinces or the three western provinces." I found him unreasonable, so I didn't talk to him. Later, I thought that they didn't know the national affairs, and it must be because of lack of knowledge. I thought that it would be best for the organs or schools in Shanghai to send people to various rural areas to give lectures on the details of the Japanese invasion of China, so that they would never import Japanese goods. In this way, it would be a little helpful for the anti-Japanese process. (And reply) If the resistance to Japanese goods only relies on Shanghai's efforts, the inland areas will not respond, and it will definitely not be effective. In the inland areas, transportation is blocked, news is relatively slow, and the harm suffered is not as great as in Shanghai, so it is expected that they will not work hard. However, people with knowledge in the inland areas must be able to understand that the tragedy that Japan staged in the Northeast this time is the prelude to extending to the inland areas. A few days ago, did Japanese sailors forcibly land at the Haizhou port? If they harass the ports along the coast and the Yangtze River, then Jiujiang and Liuhe are likely to be harmed. Do the residents of Liuhe still remember the war in Jiazi year? Jiujiang has suffered countless disasters and floods over the years. Once the Japanese soldiers suddenly arrive, the suffering will be ten times greater than before. If you want to avoid disasters and avenge your shame, you must unite as one and implement an economic boycott policy. Shanghai advocates in the front, and the inland areas respond in the back. If you persevere for a long time, the social economy will be greatly hit, and the Japanese people will complain about the rampant warlords who harm others and harm themselves. In the future, they may be a little more restrained. If you treat the Northeast incident as if it has nothing to do with me, the future strange disasters will definitely come to your own head, and it will be too late to regret it. The incoming letters will be published continuously to awaken the people in various places.

Mr. Feng Runmin Asks (Admonishing. More. Planting. Early. Wheat.) 128

Our country has suffered an unprecedented flood this year, covering as many as seventeen provinces. The rice-producing areas have all been flooded. There are great concerns about the problem of national food this year. Although the government is now borrowing wheat from the United States, I think it will not be enough in the end. Although it can be maintained in the past this year, there will still be panic next year. Now that spring ripening is about to be sown, it would be better to plant more early wheat this year, and the food in the summer of the year can reduce a worry. If you plan to plant cotton next year, I don't think it will hinder planting early wheat. I want to ask for your advice on this idea. The current period is about to plant wheat. If the time is missed, it will be useless. Therefore, I sincerely ask you to reply quickly in the newspaper.

(Reply) Your idea is very admirable, but whether there will be enough wheat next year depends on the output of various places and also on how the harvest is in foreign countries. In foreign countries, it is necessary to base on investigation statistics and use numbers to indicate the exact amount of profit and loss, and never rely entirely on ideals. I will publish the incoming letters for the attention of agricultural experts and those who are familiar with business conditions.

Weather Report 130

The Xujiahui Observatory predicted at 4:30 PM yesterday that the Yangtze River basin would be cloudy and uncertain due to the low pressure in southwestern China. The Shandong coast was sunny with strengthening westerly winds and easterly winds in the East China Sea. A hurricane was approaching the coast of Annam, with its center at 6 AM in the vicinity of 17 degrees north latitude and 108 degrees east longitude. Its direction was northwest and west. Also, the highest temperature in Shanghai in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday was 77.0 and the lowest was 67.1. The highest temperature on the same day last year was 76.1 and the lowest was 48.2.

All 131

Students Returning from Japan

More than 600 Have Returned

Since the Northeast Incident occurred, students studying in Japan have been extremely indignant. Because they could not bear the humiliation of the Japanese and felt that the national disaster was imminent, in addition to those who have successively returned to China voluntarily (more than 500), the Tokyo Institute of Technology, the Tokyo Higher Normal School, and other schools have also decided to withdraw from school and return to China. They have also jointly organized the Republic of China Students Studying in Japan Association with all Japanese students, issued a declaration, and convened representatives from various schools on September 26th to hold a general meeting at the China Youth Hall in Kanda, Tokyo. It was unanimously resolved to return to China and request travel expense subsidies from the embassy and introductions to schools for returning students from the Student Supervision Office. Therefore, more than 100 students returned to Shanghai by boat yesterday. It is also heard that they have requested admission to various national universities. It has been found that national universities have approved to accept as many students from Northeastern University as possible.

League of Nations' Results on China's Request 132

Cultural Cooperation Matters

The Chinese government requested the League of Nations on two matters concerning cultural cooperation. It was submitted to the 13th General Assembly of the International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation and other meetings on June 21st of this year and has had considerable results. Recently, the Ministry of Education translated and reported the League of Nations' document. The original report is very long. The following is a simplified record of its important points:

First, Chen Bulei, Vice Minister of Education of China, wrote to the League of Nations, inquiring about the possibility of obtaining cooperation from various appropriate agencies and departments in the International League of Nations in order to promote cultural and scientific relations between China and other member states of the League of Nations. At least the Chinese side expressed its initial views on this issue. The Vice Minister of Education proposed that it can be carried out in three directions: (A) Methods for developing cultural relations between China and other member states of the League of Nations, especially by promoting the exchange of professors, with special emphasis on those specializing in medicine, natural sciences, and law and political science. (B) Central University wants the League of Nations to help hire a professor of English literature, preferably a British person, and a professor of geography and geology each. It is best to choose from scientists from Germany, Austria, Scandinavia, or Switzerland who can teach in English (the statement stated that Central University can only send a maximum salary of 320 yuan per month for exchange professors, so assistance in other aspects is greatly expected. (C) Finally, the Minister of Education expressed his desire to establish direct relations with the agencies of the League of Nations in charge of cultural issues, and hoped to obtain detailed information on the International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation and the Education Film Society, as well as the nature of cooperation that these associations can provide to the Chinese government. The result of the association's discussion: (A) Regarding the possibility of increasing cultural relations between China and other member states of the League of Nations, the association has collected various information on existing relations and methods that can make these relations deeper and more extensive. The association's investigation cannot hope to have any results without a considerable period of time. Therefore, there is no report for the time being, but it can be said that everything is going very smoothly. (B) The association will solicit applications from professors who are willing to go to China and meet the conditions set by the Chinese government. At the same time, it will also formulate methods to fund these professors, including the term of office and the economic security that can be given to make up for the shortage of Central University's salary. (1) In terms of personnel selection, it is expected to be successful in hiring a professor of English literature. In hiring a professor of geology, after careful consideration of the qualifications of each candidate, Professor Ba Dianjiassi of the University of Geneva was recommended to the chairman. A contract will be signed soon and he can teach at Central University at the beginning of the school year. In addition, a professor of geography with German and Austrian nationality informed that Mr. Klebneit, a German professor who taught geography at Sun Yat-sen University in Guangdong for several years, is still willing to extend his stay in China and is willing to go to Central University in the name of a professor appointed by the League of Nations. All parties agreed and the letter of appointment has been sent. It is hoped that he will accept the appointment immediately. (2) With the consent of the Secretary-General of the League of Nations on the economic assistance of the League of Nations, the Association decided that the term of office of the professors in China would be two years. The League of Nations will pay 30,000 Swiss francs per year for the salary of the professors appointed under the special expenses item of the Secretary-General, including the salary sent by Central University. (To be continued)

High School Military Training Committee Requests Instruction from the Ministry of Education 134

Strictly Implement Student Volunteer Army in All Schools

Submitting Regulations for Organization to the Training Directorate-General

The Shanghai Municipal High School and Above School Military Training Committee held its second executive meeting yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM at the Zhongshan Fellow Association on Qiujiang Road. Ding Zhiying, He Liangxin, Xiao Xueyuan, Liu Fenglin, and Jiang Chaomian attended. Yu Zhongbiao, representing the Municipal Party Headquarters, was present as an observer. Jiang Chaomian chaired the meeting, and Ding Zhiying recorded the minutes. The following resolutions were passed: (1) Request the Training Directorate-General to specify the detailed organization and training plan for the Student Volunteer Army and provisionally request the Ministry of Education to issue an order to all high schools and above schools nationwide to strictly implement it. (2) Request the Training Directorate-General to stipulate the uniform of the Student Volunteer Army to achieve uniformity and enhance military bearing. (3) Regarding the matter of inviting the principals of various schools to be honorary members of the committee, Committee Member Ding will draft the letters of invitation, to be reviewed at the next meeting before being issued. (4) For schools that have not yet joined the committee, Committee Member Ding will go to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Education Bureau to investigate and notify them uniformly when the plenary meeting is convened. (5) The committee's external affairs are busy, so Committee Member Ding will hire a clerk to reside at the meeting place and handle official business full-time. (6) The committee's address will be requested from the Municipal Party Headquarters in a letter to be temporarily located within the Fourth District Party Headquarters on Qiujiang Road.

Shanghai and Hong Kong Interport Tennis Teams Split Men's and Women's Championships 136

Shanghai Men Win Championship with Complete Victory over Hong Kong, Four to Zero; Hong Kong Women Win Championship with Complete Victory over Shanghai, Five to Zero; Chinese Woman Luo Wenhui Represents Hong Kong, Men's Doubles Group Today Afternoon. The results of the Shanghai-Hong Kong interport tennis match are as follows: Shanghai men won the championship with a complete victory over Hong Kong. Hong Kong women won the championship with a complete victory over Shanghai. Although the Shanghai men's team's score was 4-0, Shanghai was undoubtedly certain to win today's doubles. The Hong Kong women's team won every match with a score of 5-0. The disparity in strength between the men's and women's teams was exactly the opposite, which is also an interesting fact. Shanghai Wins Men's Championship

One More Group Today

Today, Shanghai men won two more singles matches, bringing the total to 4-0 with a complete victory, regaining the Thai Qide Silver Cup. Luo Wenhui and Fen Que's doubles match against De Fu will be held this afternoon. Shanghai is also certain to win this match.

Jiang and He Battle for Two Hours

Tie After Tie, A Pair of Sticky Candies

Eight to Six

Jiang Daozhang (Shanghai) 6-4 He Jia (Hong Kong)

Six to Two

At the request of the Hong Kong team, the singles match between Jiang Daozhang and He Jia was held yesterday morning. The doubles match was changed to this afternoon. Although Jiang Daozhang won three straight sets, the match lasted for two hours. Almost every game ended in a tie several times before being resolved. In the first set, Jiang did not fight well, and He won four consecutive games. Jiang tied the score at 4-4, and finally resolved it at 8-6 after 5-5 and 6-6. In the second and third sets, Jiang gradually cheered up, while He did not continue. Both of them made long shots like sticky candies, but they were far from the baseline, a phenomenon of being too careful, so the interest was greatly reduced. In the second and third sets, Jiang had quite a few east-west diagonal balls. He's tactics were not inferior to Jiang, the only difference was that he used less force.

Luo Wenhui Loses to De Fu

Losing Three Straight Sets

Six to One

De Fu (Shanghai) 6-3 Luo Wenhui (Hong Kong)

Six to One

Luo Wenhui is a leader in the Hong Kong Chinese tennis world and the captain of the Hong Kong team in this interport match. She took to the court yesterday to compete against De Fu from the Shanghai team. Luo was able to cope with De Fu's fierce serves, but whenever De Fu approached the net, Luo was helpless to block left and right. Luo's forehand was powerful, and her will was calm, so she was able to find a way out in times of crisis, which was appreciated by the audience. The first and third sets were like the Yellow River bursting its banks, rushing thousands of miles, and no amount of effort could save them. In the first set, she only won one game in the fifth game, and in the third set, she only won one game in the third game. Both sets ended in failure with a score of 1-6. In the second set, she struggled slightly. Pan used clever tactics to attack left and right, and De Fu could not get close to the net, so she could not use her blocking skills. As a result, she managed to stay alive, but eventually lost with a score of 3-6.

Sometimes it was an extremely right ball, and with a wave, it became extremely left. Miss Kolaisha, at this point, sighed that she was not as good. The meeting collapsed both inside and outside, and praised her in unison, calling her the Helen Wilson Miss of China, which is really not an exaggeration. Gold Market Soars Last Week 143

Settlement Price Has Been Changed to US Exchange Rate as Standard

Swap Extended for One Month is Favorable to Short Positions

Squeeze Long Head Higher Forty-Three or Four Taels The standard gold price suddenly soared last week, fluctuating from weakness to increase and was full of turbulence. It fluctuated twenty or thirty taels a day. This was because the overseas silver market rose and then fell, especially since the settlement price has been changed to the US exchange rate as the standard. People's hearts tended to be firm, and the market price suddenly increased, almost squeezing long positions and hedging, so it suddenly rushed out of 740 taels from within 700 taels, about 70 taels in retrospect. According to statistics, it rose forty-three or four taels, so the swap was not done on October 16 of this year, but was extended for one month. Now, the mixed transaction for November and December is done, waiting for the implementation of December swapping for January starting on November 16. Only this method gives the short side a great advantage; otherwise, all short positions must be posted, and the market price is still high and very stimulating. However, this kind of situation has rarely been seen before. After that, the market situation began to be peaceful. By the weekend, both long and short sides had mutual control. As for the exchange rate, it was complicated and varied. The British pound was loose and the US dollar was tight. The gold industry generally had to pull back the shilling to flatten the position, but the US dollar was thrown out to cover the gap. It was found that the trend in the middle of this week was obviously loose and secretly tight, and the settlement price was the US exchange rate, which everyone paid attention to. At present, about 90 taels have been pressed. The recent transaction volume of the exchange is about 22,000 to 23,000 taels. Yesterday (4th), the big gap suddenly increased. Today (5th), the gold market may have changed. The following is a summary of the situation in the past six days.

There were dozens of taels of fluctuations in the market every day. Since Monday (September 28), the big gap silver suddenly shrank three pence one two five, the silver price shrank two cents two five, the shilling was extended by one level, and the domestic market was also hard. Chinese merchants pulled British pounds and threw US dollars, and the gold market opened at 688 taels, slightly less than one tael. After that, it rose immediately, and the long side turned worry into joy and the short side was greatly disappointed. It once broke through 700 taels at 03 taels. After the air was not good, it plunged more than 20 taels due to the situation at noon, totaling 677 taels and a half. The market closed well at 67 taels, totaling 84 taels and 2 qian. In the afternoon, it opened at 86 taels, reached 74 taels, and recovered to 80 taels. The exchange rate was rising, and the market closed at 75 taels and a half, continuing to decrease by 13 taels and a half compared to last Saturday. The market fluctuated by 29 taels before and after. The next day, the gap was not changed, the silver price was slightly decreased by one two five, the shilling was as before, the US dollar was extended by three seven five to squeeze the exchange rate. The domestic market was tight, and the shilling was still being pulled up, while the US dollar was being thrown out. The daily gold was also being released, mostly hedging. The standard gold price rose by 15 taels and a half at the initial opening, totaling 691 taels. It was because the big gap looked long the day before but failed, and people's hearts were rising. After that, it was 97 taels, but the selling power retreated by 10 taels, totaling 86 taels and 2 qian. The noon closing suddenly became 94 taels and 8 qian. In the afternoon, after 97 taels, the short side was greatly embarrassed due to the efforts of the big players and the motion to change the settlement price to the US dollar, and they rushed to buy in, so it reached 707 taels and a half. The closing price returned to the flat price, 703 taels and 6 qian, which was 28 taels and 1 qian higher than the previous day. The total difference in the city was 21 taels and 3 qian. The big gap on Wednesday was still unchanged, the silver market decreased by another half cent, the shilling was as before, the US dollar was listed at a larger one two five, but the domestic market was tight and rising. Because several US banks went bankrupt and India levied silver tax, people's hearts were upward. The standard gold price was initially flat at 702 taels, but the gross market shouted over 700 taels. Afterwards, the more buying, the more it rose by more than 10 taels. British and American exchange bills also rose, once reaching 731 taels. The closing price was 22 taels in the afternoon, and then 37 taels due to the sharp drop in Indian exchange, and then 35 taels and 5 qian, continuing to rise by 31 taels and 9 qian. In one day, there were 36 taels of ups and downs. Foreign and overseas Chinese had just filled the short position, and it was heard that the swap was advanced to October 5. On Thursday, the big gap shrank by 1875, the silver market was 625, the shilling was one level, the domestic market was loose, and the industry was still throwing US dollars and pulling shillings. The initial opening of the gold market was slightly increased by three taels and a half, totaling 739 taels. After a while, there were many transactions, and it plunged by more than 10 taels, totaling 22 taels. It then jumped to 40 taels due to vigorous buying. It suddenly retreated to 29 taels due to the unloading by Da Xing Yong and Dai Qiao Rifu. The noon closing was 31 taels and a half. The afternoon opening was 31 taels, followed by 26 taels and a half. The closing price was 30 taels, which was 5 taels and a half lower than the previous day. The market fluctuated by 18 taels before and after. On Friday, the big gap shrank by another 25, the US silver price increased by half a cent, the shilling remained unchanged, the US dollar was listed at a larger three seven five, and the domestic market also saw an increase. The industry was still pulling the shilling and selling the bonus. The standard gold price opened at 27 taels, a slight decrease of three taels. Afterwards, a big player, Wu, competed to buy, and the high price reached 42 taels. The noon closing was 33 taels. The afternoon was 32 taels, followed by 3 taels and 3 qian. Then, Da Xing Yong sold, and it retreated to 24 taels. The closing price was 27 taels and 7 qian, which fluctuated by 18 taels. On Saturday, the big gap was not changed, the US dollar was slightly shrunk, the shilling was as before, the US dollar was listed at a smaller half yuan, and the domestic market was mixed with British growth and US shrinkage. The gold market opened at 32 taels, an increase of 4 taels and 3 qian. It then fluctuated from 34 taels to 28 taels, with the selling side being active. Afterwards, it seemed to be rising, once reaching 36 taels. Later, the ups and downs were uncertain, but there were no large transactions on the table. The closing price was 32 taels and a half, which was 4 taels and 8 qian higher than the previous day. There were also 8 taels of ups and downs in half a day. Yesterday, we received a telegram from New York (3rd), and the US silver price also saw a slight increase of 125, with the spot price being two corners eight minutes. Securities

The Bond Market Situation Was Serious Last Week

November Futures Failed to Open

The Atmosphere Was Calm, then Fell Greatly

Last week (from September 28th to October 3rd), the bond market situation at the local Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange, apart from being closed for the first two days of the week to settle September futures, only had four market days in the entire week. Although November futures were scheduled to open after the settlement, the exchange, concerned about the current unstable market situation, required physical delivery for all November futures to limit speculative selling. Therefore, although November futures had opened, there were no transactions throughout. Even October futures saw little activity, significantly less than the previous week. The total daily trading volume was mostly less than 10 million, and on Wednesday, the trading volume was only 2.8 million, totaling only 30.52 million for the week, a decrease of over 12 million yuan compared to the previous week. This was because trading in all bonds was scarce. As for the trend of bond prices during the week, on Wednesday, due to the continuous lack of positive developments in the diplomatic situation, people felt uneasy and generally sought to sell. Therefore, all bonds, except for the 1929 and 1936 issues, were suspended from trading due to sharp declines at the opening. The situation improved slightly on Thursday, with short sellers covering their positions and some small investors buying at lower prices, pushing prices up by about three yuan. This was because it was confirmed that there was hope for a peaceful resolution with Guangdong, making the market optimistic. On Friday, the market weakened again, but the trend was relatively stable. On the last day of the week, market sentiment was weak again, and bond prices fell by about one and a half yuan. Overall, prices only rose on one of the four days, and the remaining days saw continuous declines, resulting in a significant drop compared to the previous week, ranging from three to four or five yuan. Only the 1936 issue fell by only 8 jiao and 5 fen, the Customs Duty bonds fell by 1 yuan and 8 jiao, and spot Salt Tax bonds, with no trading for a long time, fell by as much as 15 yuan compared to the opening price at the beginning of last month. Looking at the market situation, it is difficult to expect a turnaround in the short term. The following table shows the high, low, rise, and fall of bond prices for the four days (unit: yuan):

Cotton Yarn Market Firm Last Week 146

Stocks Too Depleted... Many New Long Positions

The cotton yarn market was firm last week, mainly because the anti-Japanese patriotic movement is becoming increasingly heated. Japanese yarn cannot circulate, and the sales of Chinese yarn have soared, showing a meteoric rise. Relying solely on domestic yarn is insufficient to meet demand, and the market is steadily rising. The situation is becoming increasingly tight, and short sellers are showing signs of panic. Some have had to cut their losses, causing prices to rise by five taels in two days. Later, a certain merchant, unwilling to raise prices, sold off some inventory during the涨, temporarily suppressing the market. Prices fell by two or three taels in one day. In general, stocks are too depleted, and the output of Chinese yarn is too small. When prices fall, new buyers step in again. There are rumors in the market that Indian merchants are taking long positions again, but some say that the number of purchases is very small. However, based on the overall trend, there is no possibility of a large price increase, entirely due to the shortage of goods and the inability to supply sufficient quantities. Current yarn sales are sluggish due to high prices, and there is no significant activity among merchants. The prices of standard yarn for various months are two or three taels higher than the previous week.

Chinese Cotton Market Encroached Upon by Foreign Cotton 147

American Cotton Firms Selling at Low Prices

Han Standard Cotton May Be Squeezed This Month

The American cotton market has been in a slump, with prices seemingly falling without end. The reasons for this are that the new cotton crop is increasing due to favorable weather conditions, and the global economy is sluggish, with consumption decreasing rather than increasing, making it difficult to sustain prices. New low prices are gradually emerging, breaking the 6-cent opening price. The October contract has fallen to 5.43 cents. It is difficult to determine when it will stabilize. However, the local cotton market has not been significantly affected. For October standard cotton, some Han merchants still have plans to squeeze short sellers due to the lack of supply. The forward contracts are being held up by them. However, the sales of spot cotton have been completely encroached upon by foreign cotton. American cotton is being sold at increasingly low prices, and foreign firms are willing to make special concessions. However, factories are wary of the treacherous global trends and are not daring to purchase in large quantities. In the future, both Indian and American cotton in Shanghai will face the problem of oversupply. The spot price of American cotton is only 25 taels (in the US). This cotton can be used as raw material for yarn of 32 counts or higher. Therefore, speculators and manufacturers are purchasing foreign cotton to hedge against standard cotton. Currently, this can be sustained because the supply from various regions is scarce, but in the future, there is bound to be a sharp drop in prices. American cotton is down 60 pounds from the previous week. Factories have purchased about 20,000 bales of Indian and American cotton, and very little Chinese cotton.
