Free Talk

Heartbreaking Words 149

— Du Juan

Dear fellow countrymen. Westerners have a very common slang term. When they see someone acting cowardly, they call it "Yellow." What is the relationship between this word, which originally means "yellow" in English, and "cowardly"? It's puzzling. After much contemplation, I've come up with an answer. They originally looked down on the yellow race and saw that many yellow people were cowardly. Therefore, they directly called cowardice "Yellow." However, I dare to say that this "yellow race" definitely doesn't refer to Japan. With their small three islands, they defeated our great country and then defeated powerful Russia. The spirit of "praying for death in battle" was so brave. Therefore, Westerners calling cowardice "Yellow" must refer to the 400 million citizens of our great Republic of China. My fellow countrymen, think about it, think about it again. Can you not feel heartbroken?

Miscellaneous Talks from the Non-Cultivated Hermit Studio

Pearl Necklace Congratulating Suicide (Middle) 150

Having arrived at the destination, I thought for a moment: If I die! What will my old mother's sorrow be like? What will be the pain of my wife and children? What are society's hopes and criticisms of me? Before thoroughly answering these questions, I can only temporarily endure and die later! So I ran back home, and it was already the time of the rooster's crow. My old mother was sitting there, sighing and lamenting, her eyes anxiously watching for her beloved son to return home before she could feel at ease and go to sleep. My virtuous wife was sitting next to the dim lamplight, her hands diligently sewing stitch after stitch, mending clothes, shoes, and socks for her children, husband, and mother-in-law, waiting for her husband to return. As soon as I stepped into the gate, my old mother immediately cried out, "Girl! Girl! Where have you been? You only come back at this time!" My virtuous wife said, "Why do you only come home at this time?" And they both said in unison, "Next time, come back earlier to save us from anxiously waiting and having our hearts broken and our courage shattered." Then came the inquiries about cold and warmth, asking about hunger and thirst, and then scalding hot tea was brought to my lips; hot rice was placed on the table, and they both shouted, "Eat! Eat! Eat a little!" Sometimes I would stammer and mumble a few words and go to sleep. Sometimes I wouldn't say a word and would pull the covers over my head and sleep. This happened no less than ten times. Until now, how would my old mother know that her beloved son has returned from rebirth?! How would my virtuous wife know that she is sleeping with a reanimated corpse?! Although the children are now grown adults, they were a group of little babies at the time, their soft snores making their beautiful dreams, and how would they know that they were about to become fatherless? In the end, I figured it out... dying is not enough to face the future! My old mother would faint and fall to the ground! My virtuous wife would hang herself and follow me to the underworld! My children would be displaced and homeless! Society cultivated me into an adult, but I haven't repaid society, and dying like this would be a great loss to society! I decided not to die and to live on.

Two Brave Men Who Resisted the Japanese Pirates 151

— Qing Qu

Now, the tyrannical Japanese have occupied our country and slaughtered our people. However, those in power still adhere to a policy of non-resistance, seemingly taking retreat as advancement, as if this is the only way to deal with the situation. However, the rise and fall of a nation is the responsibility of every citizen. Can our people just listen to the enemy's slaughter, endure for a moment, and sit and wait to die under the wooden clogs, gunpowder, and rain of bullets? If you are not descendants of the Yellow Emperor, I would not be surprised. Otherwise, I know that in the end, you will have the determination to save and defend yourselves. Therefore, I have examined past events and found two men in Shanghai who are truly capable of inspiring the courage to resist Japan today. Their stories are narrated below.

Mu Yilang disguised himself to scout the enemy. Mu Yilang was a Shanghai native who lived in a humble village. He made a living by begging. When the Japanese pirates arrived, he took on the task of spying. He painted his face with colorful powder and covered his body with paint, pretending to be a leper. He begged among the pirates. The pirates did not know. They associated with him. Over time, he was able to discern the number of pirates and their locations. Later, he reported this to the officials, who were prepared. He was able to annihilate them in one fell swoop. The pirates' advance was slightly curbed, largely due to the efforts of this beggar.

The Bravery of Monk Wang Sanhe. Wang Sanhe was also a Shanghai native. He was tall and strong. He learned the tofu business in the eastern town of Fahua. During the late Ming Dynasty, roving soldiers looted food. One day, they came to Wang's place and demanded soy milk. Wang pretended to agree. After a while, he lifted two seven-stone vats, filled them with water, and carried them to the edge of the shore. He tricked the soldiers into carrying them in. The soldiers looked at each other and dared not look him in the eye. They all retreated and left. They never came back. During the early Qing Dynasty, some people, posing as Japanese pirates, came from the Puhuitang and plundered. Before leaving, they forced scholars to carry their luggage. Wang was also captured. When they reached the riverbank, he glared and shouted at the pirates, "You rats! If you can defeat me with strength, I will give you the goods. Otherwise, die!" The pirates clamored and charged forward. Wang then threw their leader into the water, making gurgling sounds. Many others sank in turn until they were afraid to advance and scattered and fled. Because of this, the name of Monk Wang Sanhe shook the streets of Shanghai, and the neighborhood relied on him for safety for decades. When he died, he was buried south of Zhong'an Bridge. Later, his grave was destroyed, and some saw his body. His arm was said to have been a single bone.

Remembering Tang Weilao's Generous and Tragic Songs 152

— Wang Shaozeng

Mr. Tang Weizhi of Dachang has outstanding moral character and writing, and is highly respected in the Southeast. He once served as the president of Nanyang University and is still praised by the scholars. After becoming blind, he retired to Wuxi. Later, he founded the National College, continuing the scholarly style of Gao Gu and advocating personality education for the world. Mr. Gu, although old and feeble, has a strong spirit and is no less than the young and strong. Mr. Bu Yi eats simple vegetarian food and attends class every day, regardless of wind or snow, for more than ten years as one day. Usually, when lecturing to students, he always earnestly encourages them to restore people's hearts, avenge shame, and save the country. During the Battle of Jinan, Mr. Deng spoke on the altar and wept and sighed. He discussed the urgency of the current situation and the strategy of saving the country. Everyone present wept. At that time, there was a classmate named Xu Jun Cheng Hou, a chivalrous man. In a crowded seat, he cut his arm and wrote in blood, vowing to repay the country with death. He left a suicide note to the Anti-Japanese Alliance. Commentators were all admired. Therefore, all the students in the school tightened their belts for a month, and the surplus food was used for national skills and military training. Mr. Zeng's moral sentiment is so profound. However, Mr. Zeng often said to the students: "In the past, Zigong said, 'It is clumsy to have no intention of repaying others and causing people to suspect you. It is dangerous to have the intention of repaying others and letting people know it. It is dangerous to hear about things before they happen.' These few sentences can be called a famous theory for thousands of years. This is why the more the Vietnamese can destroy Wu. Our people know shame or not." It can be said that the words are so emotional. Mr. Once changed Yue Wumu's half-time, Jiang Hong to sing by himself. The lyrics said: "The Republic of China is ashamed. The snow has not yet fallen. Our party hates. When will it be released? Drive a long car and step through the Maguan Mountain Pass. The lofty aspirations are hungry and eat the meat of DaKuma. Laughing and talking, drinking the blood of Tanaka. Wait for the old mountains and rivers from the beginning. New China." Slightly changed the number of words. As from new casting. Its boldness and tragedy, dripping with joy. Although old, the heart is not old. It is heard that after the wine is finished, Mr. Will often sing tragically, the voice is like a bell, and the listener is terrified. Mr. Is almost a heartbroken man today. At this juncture, the mountains and rivers of the Northeast were invaded by the Japanese. Our compatriots are still unaware. How can we wake them up like Mr. One by one? (But pay)

Department Rotary Club

The Pestle of Knocking on Dreams (5) 155

— Cheng Zhanlu

"Old monk, I am deeply attached to that past peaceful era of one or two hundred years ago. Please, with your great compassion, let me sit on this revolving chair and experience that 18th-century China."

"Layman, if you wish to experience that past peace, you need only sit on the chair, and you will find yourself in its midst. However, this old monk has something to advise. China's various failures have distant causes and recent causes. I ask you to observe the distant causes. Once you sit on the chair, you will become a person of one or two hundred years ago. Do not lose your true nature. If you feel any dissatisfaction, you need only call out for the monk of the Unobstructed Hermitage, and this old monk can assist you in escaping that past environment."

"I will follow the old monk's guidance in all things."

Thus, the old monk invited Mr. Tao Chi to sit on the revolving chair. Against the Earth's rotation, he gave it a push, and the chair began to spin incessantly. Tao Chi felt dizzy and disoriented; everything disappeared. He only heard the whirring of wind in his ears! When he came to a stop and opened his eyes, he had become a newly successful scholar named Tao Chi, also sixteen years old, in Shandong Province, China, in the 18th century. Although his origins were humble, his family had been scholars for generations, and he held a respectable position in Jinan City.

It was strange! The Tao Chi who had not sat on the revolving chair was the Tao Chi with a 20th-century mindset. Once he sat on the revolving chair, he became the Tao Chi with an 18th-century old mindset. At this time, he firmly believed in the "Three Have" doctrine in books: "In books, there is a thousand Zhong of millet; in books, there are houses of gold; in books, there are faces of jade." Moreover, this "book" referred only to the narrow definition of books, specifically the Four Books, the Five Classics, and the Eight-legged Essay and model test pieces that were tools for the imperial examinations. All other books related to practical matters of state were excluded, unworthy of a glance, and deemed detrimental to success in the imperial examinations. As for what was called "science is all-powerful" and "survival of the fittest," Tao Chi had deeply studied these things before sitting on the revolving chair. Once he turned back the clock and caught up with the 18th century, Tao Chi's thoughts changed with the times! He only knew that the imperial examinations were all-powerful. He only knew that those who passed the examinations and gained official rank were the fittest, and those who failed were the failures. He knew nothing else. He had been baptized by the imperial examinations; he was a loyal believer in the Eight-legged Essay.

Go to the Battlefield 156

— Gan Yuqing

Go, to the battlefield!

The three northeastern provinces are no longer our homeland; our homeland is trapped as a battlefield for killing bandits. The battlefield is imprinted with the bloodstains of our brave warriors; the bloodstains indicate that this war is about to begin. Go, to the battlefield!

Recognize clearly, it is the mask of the imperialists. The bellies of jackals have no hearts for scorched earth. In this world, only might makes right; only from the mouths of guns can justice be spoken. Go, to the battlefield! Everything depends on our own efforts; everything depends on our own struggles. Open your eyes and see what time it is. The broadsword is held to our necks. Go, to the battlefield! Do not play tunes of despair; and do not fear how many enemies there are. Great sacrifices lead to great success; monuments must be created with flesh and blood. Go, to the battlefield! Our hot blood is boiling; our bodies are like madmen. We will use our hot blood to rust the enemy's gun barrels; we will use our bodies to plug the enemy's cannons. Go, to the battlefield! Relying on our courage, relying on our spirit of pure love, we will drive out the enemy; no, we will kill all the enemies!

September 22nd 157

— Zheng Hong

Today is the morning of September 22nd. We paced back and forth in the corridor, discussing the atrocities of the Japanese occupation of Southern Manchuria, our hearts filled with anger, as if burning and swelling within. Suddenly, we were startled by the school bell, and thought of going to the first class, of going to the lifeless algebra class. This was a class taught by a cold and emotionless old teacher. We felt great pain, forced to sit there, listening to the monotonous voice of the teacher, reciting algebraic equations, while at the same time, our hearts were burning with the Sino-Japanese Incident. This was such a contradictory situation, such an unbearable situation, yet we had to endure this imprisonment for a time.

Just then, we saw the nearly sixty-year-old teacher walking towards us in the distance, holding a roll call book and an algebra book in his hands. We became even more angry. Normally, although we disapproved of his cold and emotionless demeanor, we still pitied his old age. But today, it had turned into deep disgust. The word "puppet" burst from the mouth of one student, followed by another student's cry of "old machine." So we rushed into the classroom, sat up straight, and waited for the teacher with fiery and angry eyes. These eyes seemed to want to swallow a person whole. Indeed, in an instant, inexplicably, our old teacher had become our great enemy.

However, at the moment the old teacher stepped into the classroom doorway, we were slightly shocked. His usual dull and stiff appearance was gone; one could even say he was agile. He leaped onto the podium in two or three steps, no longer solemnly holding up the roll call book as usual. Instead, his sleepy, shy eyes, which never dared to look at us, suddenly widened, his pupils moving and radiating light. Clearly, in an instant, he had sharply looked at each and every student. What was this scene? Our nerves tightened, feeling that something was bound to happen.

He held the algebra book in his hand, his body trembling, becoming more and more severe. Suddenly, with a "thud," he placed the book on the table, followed by a sound like "crackling." He shouted the words "Compatriots!" This was a sudden attack on us. We felt the room seemed to be shaking. In our confused minds, we wondered if this was really the teacher's voice. Was this possible? That voice, originally carrying the air of the earth, had suddenly become so loud and clear. As if we were carefully watching his lips, his lips were also trembling, shouting, "Our country has reached a critical moment... has suffered great insults from the Japanese... Do you know, even a common man would draw his sword in the face of insult, let alone our four hundred million people, how can we endure the tyranny of the Japanese islands?... The great land of China, will never be a place for the Japanese to show off their military might!... Rise up, my compatriots!... We must see if justice will ultimately lose to power!"

His voice was intermittent, surging in our ears like waves. His short voice burst out with such a long string of shouts. His body seemed about to burst, flying to the ceiling. His soft, never-red face was now flushed and swollen. Sweat dripped from his bald, shiny forehead, which we usually used as talking points. In his bright red eyes, tears were also flowing. These were not tears of sorrow or fear, these were tears of excitement, these were tears of courage.

Our hearts trembled violently, and we were also shedding tears, deeply ashamed and remorseful that we had just treated him with angry eyes. These eyes could not be taken back. But at the same time, we were also shedding tears of joy, as if we had suddenly rediscovered a long-lost loved one, as if the isolated army trapped in enemy territory had suddenly had reinforcements descend from the sky. How joyful we were! Our teacher was not a puppet after all. How full of gratitude we were! Our teacher's long-lost fire of youth, was now burning again. Our teacher had truly been reborn!

At this time, we could also hear the teacher's rapid, gasping breath. Through our blurred, tearful eyes, we saw a strand of white hair at the teacher's temples being blown by the morning breeze from the parade grounds. We also saw the teacher's thin chest, in the wide long gown, rising and falling sharply. Gradually, he began to pant, followed by a fit of coughing.

A warm voice came from among us: "Teacher, rest for a while, you're overexerting yourself!"

"No! Don't look down on people! Don't mistake me for being old, thinking I'm useless... I'm still very strong, and I can still strive!"

Saying this, he patted his thin, hunched shoulders, making a "click" sound. He clenched his two fists tightly and repeated loudly,

"I'm still very strong, and I can still strive!..."

"And, besides, we are here too!"

The whole classroom rang out together.

Petition by Yunren

The wind is howling, the Huangpu River is cold.

If our goal is not achieved, we vow not to return.

A dim, green electric light reflected a strong brilliance from the surrounding white walls. Because the room was small, it appeared even brighter. Everyone else in the dormitory had gone out, leaving only a lonely me, tossing and turning in bed. Even the usually bustling dormitory – the endless sound of wooden clogs hitting the floor, the sound of water being poured in someone's room, the sound of musical instruments, the sound of laughter... all seemed to have quieted down, without a single sound.

Outside, a strong wind was blowing and heavy rain was falling. The raindrops beat against the window, rustling, further increasing the desolation of the room. Sickness oppressed me, leaving me no moment of comfort. All sorts of chaotic thoughts were constantly surging in my mind. I thought of the righteous indignation we felt a few days ago when we heard the news of the Japanese invasion of the Eastern Provinces, the enthusiastic scenes of my companions setting out to spread propaganda in the rain, the solemn attitude of the entire student body undergoing military training... one by one, they flashed through my mind in an instant. "Tap tap," a sudden knock on the door interrupted my thoughts. I gently raised my head, and Ji Yi appeared before my eyes. He was wearing a blanket from his shoulders to his waist, holding a small leather bag in his hand, like a warrior beginning his expedition.

"Has your fever gone down a bit?" he asked me when he saw me.

"The doctor already came this afternoon. He said it's a cold and fever, nothing serious. I feel much better than before now. Where are you going?" I asked him suspiciously.

"Don't you know? We are all setting off to Nanjing tonight to petition the government," he said.

"Petition?" I asked again, seemingly knowing but not knowing, because I had heard this said during the day. "It's raining heavily outside, how will you go?" I added, as if remembering something.

"The rain, we can't worry about that. Even if there are greater obstacles, we still have to do it at this time," Ji Yi looked very determined.

"Then when will you be back?" I asked lazily.

"Return date? ... We are now chanting, 'The wind is howling, the Huangpu River is cold; if our goal is not achieved, we vow not to return.' The return date is probably... uncertain," he said, and gave a faint smile.

"..........................................................................................."

Ji Yi fell silent, and I also fell silent. The two of us quietly stared at each other. Suddenly, two tears flowed from Ji Yi's eyes, shining brightly. My tears also fell.

"I'm leaving, goodbye," Ji Yi's voice trembled.

"Goodbye,"

The door slammed shut, and Ji Yi's back disappeared. My thoughts then shifted to this direction. I thought, with such fervent emotions, they are petitioning for the survival of the motherland, they will surely return with satisfaction. I also vaguely saw countless young people, with tragic hearts and ardent spirits.

Suddenly, a chorus of songs came from afar. It carried majesty and solemnity, and the words could be vaguely distinguished, "...San...Min...Zhu...Yi...Wu...Dang...Suo...Zong..." I forgot that I was a sick person, and quickly sat up, but my head felt as if it was pressed down by a great weight, throbbing violently, throbbing so much that I had to lie down again. But this majestic song, like before, continued to come, moving my heart. No, I must get up. So I endured the pain, put on my clothes, and gradually moved to the window, opened the window. The wind was very strong, and the rain beat mercilessly against my face, making me feel exceptionally cold. The dark sky had no stars. The song could now be heard very clearly, and the movement of footsteps could also be seen in the faint light on the other side of the grass. A neat sound came from the cinder road. I longed to join their ranks and move forward together, but I couldn't. Sickness bound me. Ah, this hateful sickness! Tears unknowingly covered my cheeks. They were gone, my companions were gone, they had left me alone here. Soon the sound of footsteps and the song, gradually faded, blurred, and finally disappeared at the bend in the road.

"Go forward, brave warriors! For your motherland, for your nation, go forward! I wish you success from afar!" I couldn't help but think this way, followed by a deep sigh.

Heavily and unconsciously, I fell back on the bed. The whole room was quiet again, a deathly silence all around, without the slightest sound. Only, only the clock on the table still mechanically made its impatient "tick-tock" sound.

Youth Corner

Student Soldiers 158

— Shao Guanhua

I.

Row upon row of anti-Japanese movement enthusiasm spread from the north to the south. Row upon row of cries also came from within this enthusiasm, like a quiet autumn wind, already unsettlingly vibrating. This autumn wind, like peace, gradually tended towards fervor, from fervor tended towards excitement, like a wounded wolf howling, like a comfortable tiger cub howling, a sleeping lion howling, howling, moving, and standing up.

The leaves, originally calm, now also seemed to be signaled by the autumn wind and began to shake, shooting out like arrows, reflecting the red sun of the sky.

The student soldiers of X University in West Shanghai also seemed to be triggered by the combative signal of nature and erupted. The initial humming of songs gradually lessened the consciousness of crying. The initial shrinking will gradually moved forward. The initial melancholic spirit gradually heated up. The men went up,

"Courage, Forward, Struggle," we, the student soldiers of X University in West Shanghai, were remembering, remembering like remembering something more important than eating and sleeping. Remembering while strolling, remembering while chatting, remembering while debating, remembering while silent, remembering while melancholic, remembering while angry, remembering while meditating, remembering while praying at night. These six words "Courage, Forward, Struggle," would jump up during decline, vibrate during tiredness, and shout wildly during sadness. These six words "Courage, Forward, Struggle," would writhe and coil like poisonous snakes in the minds of every student soldier.

"Is the shadow of past national humiliation not a black spot on our individual souls? Is it not a black spot on the souls of all our compatriots? Is it not a black spot on our entire nation? This black spot is what we should cut off, take away, use our shining knives to cut it off, use our guns to blast it away, use our fists to shatter it, use the hot blood from everyone's heart to scatter it. This is our responsibility, the responsibility of all the people."

This is what was on the minds of the student soldiers as they pondered and stirred.

II.

The national flag was waving.

Under the guidance of the "Assemble" command of the leaders of each squad, every student soldier stood at attention, rising from solemn contemplation.

They were all wearing yellow uniforms, leggings, each holding a gun neatly, looking at the military cap of the comrade standing on the right, staring, standing straight. "Forward march," each squad leader shouted excitedly. Each student soldier followed the front in an orderly manner. They reflected the youthful morning light as they walked forward in the morning's undulation. There was nothing to hear on the parade ground except the sound of "da, da, da" footsteps. This air of solemnity shattered the silence. They raised their heads, looked ahead, and walked step by step, forgetting their boredom, forgetting their melancholy, forgetting their sadness, forgetting their families, only remembering that they were a part of the nation, and that they should take on their responsibilities.

"Attention," each squad leader shouted sternly, and every student soldier stood still, listening to the command.

III.

The national flag was waving.

Each squad leader held a flag of white cloth with black characters, some reading "Petition the National Government in Nanjing," some reading "Rather Die Under the Knife than be a Slave to a Lost Nation," some reading "Struggle," some reading "Rise Up," some reading "Kill All Brutal Japanese," etc. Each flag showed a passionate awareness, a forward-thinking awareness. Those words were written in tears, those words were written in blood.

Each squad leader ordered the squads to count off. Each squad consisted of twenty men, totaling fifty squads. They looked at the words on the flagpoles, looking at the sky, looking at the clouds, looking at the faces of everyone forced out by the surging hot blood, looking at the trembling and angry chests of everyone.

Squad after squad, they headed towards the North Railway Station.

IV.

They set off with orderly steps, treading on dust on the road, singing songs. Their songs were calm, organized. Within their calm, organized songs, the tones were tragic and indignant. That song was the fluctuating cry of everyone's inspiration, suddenly rising, suddenly falling, spinning and leaping in the swaying of the wind. Suddenly they turned coarse and violent, like the tides of a stormy coast. They unknowingly had reached the North Railway Station.

They forgot fatigue, forgot hunger, they felt that the present moment did not allow them to have such emotions, they understood that the present moment only allowed them to muse on their own "mission," this "mission" that could not be delayed.

They had already boarded the train, they sat separately in squads, they did not think that many pedestrians were noisily criticizing them, praising them, they did not think that "life" and "death" were joyful and sad, they thought of those six words "Courage, Forward, Struggle."

Social News

Japanese Residents and the Philippine Hill Bin Existence 159

Japan, with its small land and overpopulation, has no choice but to develop outwards. In order to solve its overpopulation problem, Japan has so-called "Northern Expansion" and "Southern Expansion" policies. However, European and American countries have already expelled Japanese residents from their territories. The only places where Japan can extend its reach are some parts of Asia. For decades, Japan has been meticulously planning to seize our country's Northeast (Manchuria) and the South Seas islands. Now, Japan has already implemented military action by occupying Shenyang. Newspapers have exposed its ambitions. What I want to discuss here is the Japanese residents' conspiracy to buy the Philippines. 丨丨

According to the Philippine correspondence, the Philippine Free Press published on the 18th of last month contained important documents treasured for fifteen years regarding Japanese residents' plan to purchase the Philippines with 400 million yen. The origin is that in 1916, a group of 61 Japanese celebrities including Dr. Seiichi Kishida traveled to the Philippines and were well received. At that time, Japanese celebrities residing in the Philippines and Japanese celebrities visiting the Philippines gathered to draft a petition to then-Prime Minister Ōkuma, suggesting that the Japanese government use 400 million yen to buy the Philippines from the United States. Unexpectedly, the original manuscript of the petition was obtained by a patriotic youth of the Philippines. That youth was a servant of a certain Japanese residents' organization in the Philippines, so he was able to obtain this original manuscript. After obtaining this original manuscript, he immediately handed it over to the Free Press and sent a copy to Mr. Quezon, the Philippine commissioner to the United States at the time. After obtaining the document, the Free Press kept it secret for a long time. Recently, the issue of Japanese residents in Davao has attracted attention from all parties in the Philippines, so the newspaper published this fifteen-year-old document to make the public aware that the Japanese invasion of the Philippines has been premeditated for a long time, and not a sudden event. Now, the original manuscript of the Japanese residents' petition is translated as follows: (1) The situation in the Far East,

We dare not predict when the European war will end and what the conditions for restoring peace will be in the future (Translator's note: Because the European war was in full swing at that time, hence this statement), but it can be asserted that Germany will lose its influence in the Far East. The balance of power in the Eastern Hemisphere has formed a new trend. Russia, with its long railways, has consolidated itself in the north. Britain, with India and Australia as its bases, is also very secure. These two countries are both allies of our country (Japan's ally, Translator's note: At that time, the Russian Tsarist government had not yet been overthrown). At present, they are not a threat to our country. France is focusing on managing its Indochina (Annam), which is also not a threat to Japan. Only the islands owned by the United States, scattered in the Pacific Ocean, such as Honolulu, the Philippines, and Guam, will undoubtedly lead to conflicts of interest with Japan in the future. If any major power has a dispute with the Japanese Empire, if the Chinese issue is the main cause of the dispute, then Japan's only major enemy should be the United States. Recently, the United States Congress has expressed unfriendly sentiments towards Japan, which is clear evidence.

(2) The China Issue

As for the China issue, the European war has indeed given us the opportunity to develop our interests in China, but it is also enough to make American politicians engage in conspiracies to harm our interests. Moreover, our development in the South Seas easily causes panic among Americans regarding the Philippines. This phenomenon is not surprising, because recently, there have been very serious disputes between Japan and the United States over the issue of the treatment of Japanese residents in the Pacific by the United States. Fortunately, this dispute has not reached the point of rupture, but it has already caused a lot of suspicion and resentment between the two countries. If American politicians oppose Japan's China policy and engage in various conspiracies to undermine it, what other incidents cannot occur between the two countries once the conspiracy expands? Moreover, after the European war ends, no matter how it ends, we firmly believe that Germany will use the United States to encourage China to oppose Japan, because after the war, Germany will have no ability to directly interfere in Far Eastern affairs.

(4) Methods of Maintaining Peace If the true meaning of diplomacy lies in avoiding war, then shouldn't we try our best to find a peaceful way to resolve the dispute between Japan and the United States? The dispute between Japan and the United States is based on the rapid increase in the Japanese population. The Japanese population increases by 600,000 every year (Translator's note: Currently, the Japanese population increases by 1.3 million every year), and there must be a place to settle. The United States has a vast land and a sparse population, and needs Japanese workers. However, American workers have a strong organization and are determined to exclude Japanese workers. Therefore, political organizations are deployed to implement their plans. We know that the central government of the United States does not agree, but the states of the United States have independent powers. The federal government cannot stop what the state governments do. Although our country sympathizes with the US federal government, it still cannot abandon the demand for fair treatment of Japanese residents and equal opportunities. Under such circumstances, it is not easy to resolve. However, there is still a glimmer of hope.

(4) The Philippines as the Focus of American Political Strife After the United States occupied the Philippines in 1898, the Philippines became the focus of American political strife. If the United States occupies the Philippines for a long time, it will inevitably go against the American spirit. First-class American politicians such as Wilson have already strongly advocated abandoning the Philippines. At this time, the US government is led by the Democratic Party. President Wilson and other key figures of the Democratic Party, and a small number of key figures of the Republican Party, do not consider colonial policy to be correct, and advocate abandoning their possessions in the Far East. What the United States does not need and is willing to abandon may be the key to resolving the friendship between Japan and the United States.

(5) Suggestions to the Prime Minister

What we want to suggest to the Prime Minister is nothing more than that the Japanese government should consult with the US government to buy the Philippines from the United States at a certain price, repay the loan in installments, and use the dispatch of Japanese labor to the United States as an exchange condition. If this proposal can be realized, all disputes between the two countries will naturally come to an end. The United States can thereby reduce its "burden of the Japanese," and Japan can thereby alleviate its "overpopulation." It is a win-win situation. What is there for both countries not to do?

Leaders in the American political circles can often maintain their fairness and goodwill towards other countries. Although they have recently embarked on the wrong path of expanding their territory, the recent victory of the Democratic Party in the election and the control of the government's power show that the United States has returned to its inherent political track.

(6) Commercial Issues with China The United States has a vast land and abundant resources, and its products must be exported for sale. China is one of its main markets. Looking at the United States in Europe, it does not have an inch of territory, but it can still gain commercial power. It is obvious that the Americans already know that they do not need the Philippines as a base for their trade with China. Japan has long advocated maintaining the integrity of China's territory and is determined to abide by the Open Door Policy in China, so that all countries can enjoy equal opportunities in China. Therefore, the United States' abandonment of the Philippines will not result in the loss of its commercial development on the Asian continent. The United States has always been committed to maintaining peace and humanity. If it insists on occupying its distant possessions, it must arouse suspicion from other countries, and it will be said that it has ulterior motives other than commerce. We dare to say that Americans who understand the truth will never regard occupying the Philippines as a necessary condition for developing Far Eastern commerce. If the United States receives a reasonable reward, it will be willing to abandon the Philippines to reduce its burden. It should be noted that the United States is waiting for a reasonable opportunity and reason to abandon the Philippines.

(7) The Value of the Philippines

If the United States agrees to our plan, then what is the value of the Philippines? This should be carefully calculated by those responsible for the consultation. However, we may as well make an estimate first. According to the war between the United States and Spain, it cost a total of 130 million US dollars. The bonds issued by the United States at that time were 200 million US dollars, with an annual interest rate of 3%. However, the actual money spent during the war did not exceed 130 million US dollars. After the war, the United States signed a treaty and bought the Philippines from Spain for 20 million US dollars. After the Americans occupied the Philippines, they spent another 7 million US dollars to buy the Catholic Church's real estate in the Philippines, 5 million US dollars to build wharves, bridges, and roads, and 4 million US dollars to build the water reservoir in Manila.

In 1910, the US-owned Philippine government sold 123,680 hectares of church land out of 397,000 hectares to the people (approximately one-third). Moreover, the 130 million US dollars in war expenses for the Spanish-American War were not purely for the conquest of the Philippines. After the Spanish-American War, the United States obtained not only the Philippines but also Puerto Rico and Cuba as protectorates. It is estimated that the Philippines currently has 493 miles of railways. If Japan buys from the United States, the value is no more than 70 million US dollars. Excluding the cost of the British railways, the total price for Japan to buy the Philippines from the United States should not exceed 400 million yen. A cheaper price may be obtained during formal consultations in the future.

(8) The Benefits to Japan

If Japan acquires the Philippines, its benefits will be no less than those to the United States. The Philippines is only 62 miles away from Taiwan, so Japan has a necessary to purchase it. Moreover, the Caroline Islands in the South Seas have recently fallen into Japanese hands. The current situation makes it necessary for Japan to advance in two directions. Our governance of Taiwan has won the praise and admiration of the world. If we obtain the Philippines, we will also be able to govern the Philippines in the same way as we govern Taiwan. Administrative efficiency, the revitalization of industry, the treatment of the natives, and the provision of sanitation will all be the same as in Taiwan. Once the Philippines is obtained by Japan, the coast of the Asian continent will have a connected chain of Japanese islands as a barrier, from the Ryukyu Islands in the north to the Caroline Islands in the south. Then the territory of China can be complete, and the permanent peace of East Asia can be realized. If we can encourage Americans' love of justice and peace, we will be able to obtain American sympathy, because once Japan and the United States break apart, the magnitude of the disaster is difficult to describe. Although we now possess the Caroline Islands in the South Seas, a war with the United States is certainly not difficult, but why spend a huge sum of 300 to 400 million yen to occupy the Philippines more easily? What is gained is land, and what is spent is only money. If Japan can buy the Philippines from the United States through peaceful means, both the United States and Japan will benefit. Isn't it better than war?

Conclusion

Japanese residents seem to think that by spending only 300 to 400 million yen, they can buy the Philippines from the United States. If that were possible, why would the United States have gone to war with Spain and occupied the Philippines? After the military victory, why would it have spent such a large sum of money to buy the Philippines from Spain and build it? The United States, as a kingdom of money, is probably contemptuous of Japan's shabby 300 to 400 million yen.

The most absurd thing Japanese residents say is that "Japan has long advocated the integrity of its territory and is determined to abide by the Open Door Policy in China, so that all countries can enjoy equal opportunities in China," and "Then the territory of China can be complete, and the permanent peace of East Asia can be realized." 丨丨 Today, it is not Britain, France, or the United States, nor is it Russia, that has occupied Shenyang, but Japan, which claims to advocate the integrity of China's territory. It is not another country that is destroying the permanent peace of East Asia, but Japan, which constantly claims to maintain the permanent peace of East Asia. Get out! Our China has not yet become a colony. We want our nation to stand up on its own. We want to seal your mouths, you Japanese and Americans, who shout the slogans of "Open Door Policy, Equal Opportunities."

Finally, Japan, Japan, is capable of seizing the land of others. After all, if World War II breaks out, its small gambling capital of land will probably be bet on its ambition to seize the land of others. French General Foch

European War Diary Translated by Gu Angruo 160

(1) The French army group is attacking towards Brussels, with the right wing advancing to Beek on the Schilde River, and the attack on Lesinne on the Dender River. In the attack, it is necessary to first control important waterways such as the Schilde River and the Dender River. If necessary, the British army can join in and flank. (2) The British army (5th, 3rd, 1st, and 4th armies) is attacking south of the Beek, Lesinne, and Halle lines. The right wing is attacking Archie Mount via Vleteren and Phillippe. The British army still has the task of repelling the enemy to the Ardennes Mountains, while assisting the Franders army group in crossing the Schilde and Dender Rivers to avoid hindering the future. The 1st French Army is also assisting the British army in combat.

(3) The French army (1st, 10th, 5th, and 4th armies) and the 1st American Army are fighting south of the Beek, Lesinne, and Halle lines. The 1st French Army is attacking La Goupille and Chimay to cover the British army, while the right wing is attacking the Selci-Somme line. The 5th and 4th French armies and the 1st American Army are advancing to the Mezières, Sedan, and Meuse River areas to secure the Aisne River defense line on both the left and right wings. The left wing (5th French Army) is advancing towards Barisey, and the right wing (4th French and 1st American armies) is advancing towards Buzancy-lès-Chis.

Social News Manuscript Guidelines 161

(1) The text should be related to domestic and foreign science, industry, commerce, rural areas (2) Hygiene, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life news. The white drawing is limited to various lyrical expressions about social life. (3) Photographs should be qualified for seasonality, scenery, animals and plants, and news photography. Female models in seasonal and landscape photography are especially welcome.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(5) Do not write horizontally, do not write carelessly, and save words as much as possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not draw pictures with blue ink, and do not use colored paper. Use limited black drawing paper.

(8) Please indicate "Social News Editorial Department" for submissions.
